work</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">Besides, electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) are performed to better understand the superior rate performance of the in situ carbon-coated NVPF nanosheets for sodium energy storage with frequencies ranging from 0.01 Hz to 100 kHz. The Nyquist plots of the NVPFC-NS and NVPF-NP electrodes are all made up of a semicircle in the high-frequency range and a sloped straight line in the low-frequency range, corresponding to the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and Warburg impedance, respectively. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/suppl_file/am2c07897_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>, the NVPFC-NS electrode displays a smaller <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (84.5 Ω) than that of the NVPF-NP electrode (129.5 Ω), while a steeper line than that of the NVPF-NP electrode, suggesting the NVPFC-NS possesses a faster charge transfer and reduced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion impedance, which can be ascribed to the mesoporous structured NVPFC-NS with a relatively high surface area facilitating charge transfer between active material and electrolyte, and in situ carbon-coated nanosheets prompting fast transports of both electrons and Na<sup>+</sup>.</div><div class="NLM_p">Considering the advantages of NVPFC-NS discussed above, it was used as the cathode to pair up porous carbon (PC) as the anode to fabricate full cells. The porous carbon anode material was synthetized by using modified polyacrylonitrile as the carbon source. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> The current density and specific capacity of the full cell shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a,d are all based on the mass of NVPFC-NS. Following conventions, the desodiation process of NVPFC-NS is defined to be charged, and the sodiation process is defined to be discharged. The galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a demonstrate three sloping stages suggesting a combination effect from both the intercalation cathode and the pseudocapacitive anode. The overlapped charge–discharge profiles of the initial three cycles illustrate the excellent reversibility of NVPFC-NS//PC full cells and display a remarkably reversible capacity of 109 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>. Notably, the charge capacity increases from the first to the second cycle due to further activation of the material. Considering that the capacity mismatch between the two electrodes will affect the full cell’s performance, the mass ratio of the active material for the cathode and anode should be optimized. For achieving the highest energy/power density, this mass ratio is determined to be 1.5:1 according to the result shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b (all the data are obtained based on this mass ratio). The Ragone plot with a mass ratio of 1.5:1 also reveals the relationship between energy and power density. As expected, the assembled NVPFC-NS//PC fuel cell delivers a maximum energy density of 94.8 W h kg<sup>–1</sup> at a low power density of 155.4 W kg<sup>–1</sup>. As power density increases to 7295 W kg<sup>–1</sup>, the energy density of this full cell can still reach 44.5 W h kg<sup>–1</sup>. Note that the energy and power densities of the full cells were all calculated based on the active materials in both electrodes by <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="eqs 1">eqs 1</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="2">2</a> (see <a class="ref internalNav" href="#sec2" aria-label="Experimental Section">Experimental Section</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> More importantly, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>c, apart from the power density can get to an appropriate value, which can rival the power density of supercapacitors, our assembled full cell still maintains the comparable energy density of traditional lithium-ion batteries. We also compare the Ragone plots of NVPFC-NS//PC full cells with other reported Na-ion storage devices (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/suppl_file/am2c07897_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>). As disclosed, our device exhibits the highest energy and power densities in comparison to others. Moreover, the charge/discharge capacity of the full cell was maintained at about 61 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> even after 200 cycles at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>(<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>d), achieving a capacity retention of 93.7% during the entire cycle process, demonstrating a relatively stable cycling performance. The electrochemical performance of full cells based on NVPF-NP//PC is also provided shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/suppl_file/am2c07897_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>. Three pairs of charge–discharge platforms can still be observed in continuous slope galvanostatic charge/discharge profiles, indicating the electrochemical properties of cathode and anode electrodes are displayed simultaneously. However, the NVPF-NP//PC full cell displays a poorer cycling performance than that of the NVPFC-NS//PC full cell, only less than 40 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> capacity can be obtained after 200 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Finally, we evaluated the performance of the device in tentative applications by driving a mini fan. After fast charging to 3.8 V, a single sodium-ion full cell was able to drive a mini fan (inset of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>b, Video S1, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/suppl_file/am2c07897_si_002.mp4" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>), which suggests the high-power output of this full cell for practical applications.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/asset/images/medium/am2c07897_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/asset/images/large/am2c07897_0007.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Electrochemical performance of full cells based on NVPFC-NS//PC. (a) Galvanostatic charge–discharge profiles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup> in the voltage of 1.0–3.8 V. (b) Ragone plots of these full cells with different mass ratios of the active material in the cathode (NVPFC-NS) versus that in the anode (PC). (c) Device-based performance for the currently available energy-storage systems. (d) Cycling performance at 1000 mA g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c07897/asset/images/large/am2c07897_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.2c07897&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, we have demonstrated a low-cost and scalable amylopectin-assisted synthesis of in situ carbon-coated NVPF nanosheet-constructed 3D cathode material, where the amylopectin functions as both an organic carbon source and structure direction agent. Electrochemical tests of the obtained sample exhibit good electrochemical performance for sodium storage, especially in terms of the superior rate capability (93 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 60 C, 51 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 150 C) as well as long cycling stability (≈93% capacity retention over 500 cycles at 10 C), because its unique in situ carbon-coated 2D nanostructure shorten the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion length and endows the composites with effective electron transport. Moreover, when applied to full cells, it still demonstrates a remarkably high energy density of 94.8 W h kg<sup>–1</sup> and a power density of 7295 W kg<sup>–1</sup> with excellent cycling performance in the voltage range of 1.0–3.8 V. Hence, we are successful in not only providing a strategy to obtain a 2D nanostructure material with complicated multicomponent but also in fabricating high power Na-ion full cell to promote the practicability and commercialization of SIBs, leading to their real applications in the future.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of current scientific issues underpinning Li batteries and elec. double-layer capacitors.  Energy-storage technologies, including elec. double-layer capacitors and rechargeable batteries, have attracted significant attention for applications in portable electronic devices, elec. vehicles, bulk electricity storage at power stations, and load leveling of renewable sources, such as solar energy and wind power.  Transforming Li batteries and elec. double-layer capacitors requires a step change in the science underpinning these devices, including the discovery of new materials, new electrochem., and an increased understanding of the processes on which the devices depend.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200026"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, S.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Seo, D.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ceder, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode Materials for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries: Potential Alternatives to Current Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries: potential alternatives to current lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Sung-Wook; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Lithium (Li)-ion batteries (LIB) have governed the current worldwide rechargeable battery market due to their outstanding energy and power capability.  In particular, the LIB's role in enabling elec. vehicles (EVs) has been highlighted to replace the current oil-driven vehicles in order to reduce the usage of oil resources and generation of CO2 gases.  Unlike Li, sodium is one of the more abundant elements on Earth and exhibits similar chem. properties to Li, indicating that Na chem. could be applied to a similar battery system.  In the 1970s-80s, both Na-ion and Li-ion electrodes were investigated, but the higher energy d. of Li-ion cells made them more applicable to small, portable electronic devices, and research efforts for rechargeable batteries have been mainly concd. on LIB since then.  Recently, research interest in Na-ion batteries (NIB) has been resurrected, driven by new applications with requirements different from those in portable electronics, and to address the concern on Li abundance.  In this article, both neg. and pos. electrode materials in NIB are briefly reviewed.  While the voltage is generally lower and the vol. change upon Na removal or insertion is larger for Na-intercalation electrodes, compared to their Li equiv., the power capability can vary depending on the crystal structures.  It is concluded that cost-effective NIB can partially replace LIB, but requires further investigation and improvement.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref4" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201206854"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As a promising alternative to the market-leading lithium-ion batteries, low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are attractive for applications such as large-scale elec. energy storage systems.  The energy d., cycling life, and rate performance of SIBs are fundamentally dependent on dynamic physiochem. reactions, structural change, and morphol. evolution.  Therefore, it is essential to holistically understand SIBs reaction processes, degrdn. mechanisms, and thermal/mech. behaviors in complex working environments.  The recent developments of advanced in situ and operando characterization enable the establishment of the structure- processing- property- performance relationship in SIBs under operating conditions.  This Review summarizes significant recent progress in SIBs exploiting in situ and operando techniques based on X-ray and electron analyses at different time and length scales.  Through the combination of spectroscopy, imaging, and diffraction, local and global changes in SIBs can be elucidated for improving materials design.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref8" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c04482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palanisamy, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reddy Boddu, V.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A sol-gel process followed by heat treatment derived a layered P2-type NaCoO2 cathode, which depicted unit cell parameters values of a = 2.8389 Å, c = 10.9899 Å, and V = 76.71 Å3 in powder X-ray diffraction pattern.  The synthesized cathode exhibited hexagonal, 2D platelets with an ~ 300 nm thickness.  During the anodic and cathodic sweeps, the cyclic voltammograms revealed multiple redox peaks with the same current densities, shapes, and peak positions, assocd. with the highly reversible phase transition mechanism of the layered P2-type NaCoO2 cathode.  The sodium cells yielded the capacities of 93/92 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C and 87/87 mAh g-1 at 1 C for the 50th charge-discharge cycles.  The in situ multimode calorimetry (MMC) studies of sodium cells demonstrated a thermal explosion event, which occurred by sodium melting, short-circuit, electrode decompn. reaction, gas generation, exothermic reaction, released heat energy, and cell gasket melting.  Ultimately, the calcd. released total heat energies of ~ 550/740 J g-1 for in situ MMC studies and ~ 312/594 J g-1 for ex situ DSC analyses (charge state at 4 V and discharge state at 2 V) show that the discharged state of sodiated layered P2-type NaCoO2 cathode material is more unsafe than the charge state.  Furthermore, the ex situ differential scanning calorimetry (DSC) spectrum of a discharge state at 2 V of layered P2-type NaCoO2 revealed a decreased onset temp. (DOT) at 141°C with two pronounced exothermic peaks at 197 and 266°C with a released higher total heat energy of 594 J g-1 than the charge state heat energy at 312 J g-1, attributed to the higher charge onset temp. (COT) at 191°C.  Thus, the obsd. higher heat energy and decreased onset temp. for the discharge state at 2 V is assocd. with the higher Na+ ion in the discharge state of the layered P2-type NaxCoO2 cathode than that of the pristine cathode, showcasing that the layered P2-type NaCoO2 cathode is unsafe at the discharged condition for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref9" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1039/c5ta05205j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stable Layered P3/P2 Na<sub>0.66</sub>Co<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have captured widespread attention for grid-scale energy storage owing to the natural abundance of sodium. How the compn. dets. the structural chem. is decisive for the electrochem. performance but very challenging to predict, esp. for complex compns. Herein, we develop a simple and convenient self-template method to prep. a hollow-structured Prussian blue analog (CoFe-PBA).  This structure is conducive to buffer the vol. changes during ion extn. and insertion processes and shorten the ion diffusion path.  When further building a thin polydopamine (PDA) coating, the synthesized CoFe-PBA@PDA exhibits a high discharge capacity of 123.1 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 71.5% after 500 cycles. Prussian blue analogs (PBAs) are broadly recognized as promising cathode materials due to their low cost, high theor. capacity, and cycling stability, although they suffer from low-crystallinity-induced performance deterioration.  Herein, a facile "ice-assisted" strategy is presented to prep. highly crystd. PBAs without any additives.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Buckwheat derived N-doped carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 enwrapping in graphene as enhanced cathode material for high performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Junke; Wang, Hao; Zhang, Hongwei; Wu, Shugen; Wang, Wei; Zou, Liang; Jin, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">516</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">230654</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) is one of the Na-contg. superionic conducting crystals, but it has a disadvantage of low intrinsic electronic cond.  To improve this issue, NVPF@C/G with a three-dimensional conductive structure from bio-carbon (buckwheat) and graphene is fabricated via a straightforward carbothermal redn. method.  We use this material to construct cathodes for Na-ion batteries.  The resulting NVPF@C/G delivers high initial (equal to 137.5 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C) and stable long-term (equal to 110.5 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles) capacity.  At 10 C, the capacity of the NVPF@C/G-contg. cathode is 80.6 mAh g-1.  Furthermore, a Na-ion full-cell contg. our NVPF@C/G-based cathode and hard carbon anode shows outstanding cycling stability with the initial discharge capacity of 101.6 mAh g-1.  The discharge capacity of this full cell returns to 90.4 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C after it is tested at various high rates.  Such superior performances can be attributed to the 3D conductive network in NVPF@C/G, which can increase the cond. and improve the kinetics of the Na3V2(PO4)2F3.  This work suggests that the buckwheat-derived carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 enwrapped in graphene can be a potential active material for high rate and long-cycle Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/d0ta00130a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Well-dispersed Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO with improved kinetics for high-power sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Feng; Zhao, Yifei; Xia, Lishuang; Yang, Zhendong; Wei, Jinping; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Polyanion-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 with high potential is regarded as a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it usually shows low electronic and ionic cond., further leading to inferior rate capability.  Here well-dispersed Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles were anchored on reduced graphene oxide (rGO) via a facile pptn. process in an isopropanol-water mixed solvent.  The Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO composite exhibited apparently improved kinetics and further delivered high reversible capacity and outstanding high-rate performance.  Furthermore, sodium-ion full cells composed of Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO cathodes and hard carbon anodes presented high power d.  This work offers a simple and scalable approach to boost the kinetics of polyanion-type cathodes for high-power alkali-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201800215"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Broux, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fauth, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hall, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chatillon, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bianchini, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bamine, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Leriche, J.-B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Suard, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carlier, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reynier, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Simonin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Masquelier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Croguennec, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Rate Performance for Carbon-Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> in Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1800215</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Rate Performance for Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 in Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Broux, Thibault; Fauth, Francois; Hall, Nikita; Chatillon, Yohann; Bianchini, Matteo; Bamine, Tahya; Leriche, Jean-Bernard; Suard, Emmanuelle; Carlier, Dany; Reynier, Yvan; Simonin, Loic; Masquelier, Christian; Croguennec, Laurence</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. and structural properties of a series of three different Na3V2(PO4)2F3 samples (with or without carbon coatings of different natures), obtained via different synthesis methods, are compared through operando high-resoln. synchrotron X-ray diffraction.  The pristine materials all possess negligible quantities of oxygen defects, as probed by the b/a lattice parameters ratios and solid-state NMR.  Operando X-ray diffraction recorded during charge at C/2 reveals subtle differences between the samples (of different particle size, morphol., and carbon-coating nature) in the crystallinity of the intermediate compns. formed within the Na3V2(PO4)2F3-NaV2(PO4)2F3 phase diagram.  A new temp.-controlled operando cell is used to det. this phase diagram at 0°C, mostly unchanged compared to that of recorded at 25°C.  Very high charging and discharging rates are demonstrated and intermediate compns. can be spotted operando even up to 25 C rate at which the compositional phase diagram is only slightly altered compared to that recorded under equil. conditions.  Optimized carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 shows exceptional rate and electrochem. cycling capabilities, as demonstrated by hard carbon//Na3V2(PO4)2F3 18650 prototypes of 75 Wh kg-1 that can be charged or discharged 4000 times at 1 C rate.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202201719"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, R.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic Effect, Structural and Morphology Evolution, and Doping Mechanism of Spherical Br-Doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C toward Enhanced Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhuang; Zhang, Ruijie; Fan, Changling; Liu, Xunlin; Gao, Peng; Zhang, Weihua; Liu, Zhixiao; Han, Shaochang; Liu, Jinshui; Liu, Jilei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2201719</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 has attracted wide attention due to its high voltage platform, and stable crystal structure.  However, its application is limited by the low electronic cond. and the ease formation of impurity.  In this paper, the spherical Br-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C is successfully obtained by a one-step spray drying technol.  The hard template polytetrafluoroethylene (PTFE) supplements the loss of fluorine, forming porous structure that accelerates the infiltration of electrolyte.  The soft template cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) enables doping of bromine and can also control the fluorine content, meanwhile, the self-assembly effect strengthens the structure and refines the size of spherical particles.  The loss, compensation, and regulation mechanism of fluorine are investigated.  The Br-doped Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C sphere exhibits superior rate capability with the capacities of 116.1, 105.1, and 95.2 mAh g-1 at 1, 10, and 30 C, and excellent cyclic performance with 98.3% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 10 C.  The d. functional theory (DFT) calcn. shows weakened charge localization and enhanced cond., meanwhile the diffusion energy barrier of sodium ions is reduced with Br doping.  This paper proposes a strategy to construct fluorine-contg. polyanions cathode, which enables the precise regulation of structure and morphol., thus leading to superior electrochem. performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2021.01.029"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are the primary candidate for a low-cost and resource-abundant alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale elec. storage applications.  However, the development of sodium-ion batteries is hindered by the lack of suitable cathode materials that have sufficient specific energy d. and cycle life.  Here, we report layered NaVOPO4 as a cathode material that exhibits high voltage (∼3.5 V vs. Na/Na+), high discharge capacity (144 mAh g-1 at 0.05 C), and remarkable cyclability with 67% capacity retention over 1,000 cycles.  The excellent performances result from the high Na+ ion diffusion rate in the two-dimensional path and the reversible transformation behavior of (de)sodiation.  Particularly, this layered structure and its synthetic procedure can be extended to other alkali-metal intercalation materials, leading to other metal-ion battery systems, which opens a new avenue for large-scale energy storage systems with the development of high-energy-d. and long-life cathodes for elec. storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.135533"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational design of two dimensional single crystalline Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets for boosting Na+ migration and mitigating grain pulverization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xin; Wu, Qiao; Guo, Peng; Liu, Xiaojie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received considerable attention as stationary energy storage applications.  However, it is still a challenge to develop high energy d. and stable cathode materials for SIBs.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3, as one of the most promising polyanion-type cathodes, has been explored due to its high reversible capacity and high discharge voltage.  In spite of excellent intrinsic features, poor rate capability ascribed to the intrinsically low electronic cond. and unsatisfactory ion cond., as well as grain pulverization, severely hinders their practical applications.  Based on d. functional theory calcns. and common knowledge about two dimensional materials, it is believed that rational design of two dimensional single cryst. Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanosheets could be an effective route to enhance Na+ migration and mitigate grain pulverization for high-performance SIBs.  Besides, combing Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and three-dimensional porous carbon, a composite of two dimensional Na3V2(PO4)2F3 wrapped with three dimensional porous carbon, was synthesized and utilized as cathode for SIBs.  When evaluated as cathode, NVPF@3Dc exhibits a high specific capacity of 131.5 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C, excellent rate property of 65.7 mAh g-1 at 10 C, and long lifespan of 2500 cycles with the capacity of 51.6 mAh g-1 at 5 C.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.7b00927"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High Power-High Energy Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Sodium Cathode: Investigation of Transport Parameters, Rational Design and Realization</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Wu, Chao; Chen, Chia-Chin; Kopold, Peter; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are realistic and promising alternatives to lithium due to the abundance of Na and the similar intercalation chem. of Na when compared to the lithium counterpart.  Developing high-power and high-energy sodium batteries is still a significant challenge.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has been shown to combine excellent charge-discharge kinetics with a competitively high voltage.  However, the major issue is, as for the vast majority of electrode materials, the lack of distinct knowledge of fundamental transport parameters, on which an optimized strategy for developing a high-power and high-energy sodium cathode can be based.  This work aims at filling this gap.  We exptl. investigate the intrinsic ionic and electronic conductivities, as well as the chem. diffusion coeff. of sodium of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 by impedance and dc polarization.  On the basis of these results, we develop an optimized design.  As the electronic cond. is found to be much smaller than the ionic one, electronic wiring of the particles (by a graphene network) has higher priority than providing electrolyte contact.  This is important since the contact by graphene and electrolyte wetting is partly antagonistic, not so much because of interfacial tensions rather because of the introduced heterogeneities on the nanoscale (cf. Lotus effect).  We develop and apply a one-step cost-effective low temp. hydrothermal method without any postheat treatment for the fabrication of a nanoparticulate (∼30-50 nm) NVPF electrode, which provides sufficient porosity and in which every nanoparticle is connected to the graphene network.  In terms of rate capability, the performance of this electrode is excellent and at least belongs to the best Na storage performances reported for Na3V2(PO4)2F3 so far.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2019.123952"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-situ constructing Na3V2(PO4)2F3/carbon nanocubes for fast ion diffusion with high-performance Na+-storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunsha; Liang, Xinghui; Chen, Guilin; Zhong, Wentao; Deng, Qiang; Zheng, Fenghua; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin; Hu, Junhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core/Double-Shell Structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C Nanocomposite as the High Power and Long Lifespan Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiang; Meng, Xing; Wei, Zhixuan; Wang, Dongxue; Gao, Yu; Wei, Yingjin; Du, Fei; Chen, Gang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

These superior electrochem. performances remained stable when the Na3V2(PO4)2F3@CD cathode was used in a full cell, suggesting a promising application of the material for high rate and long lifespan Na-ion batteries.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ redox reaction induced firmly anchoring of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 on reduced graphene oxide &amp; carbon nanosheets as cathodes for high stable sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yue; Wang, Ting; Tang, Yakun; Huang, Yudai; Jia, Dianzeng; Guo, Yong; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is considered as one of the most promising cathodes for sodium-ion batteries due to its high operating potential, fast ion transport and superior structural stability.  However, its poor rate capability and insufficient cyclability hinder its future practical applications.  Herein, a hybrid of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles firmly anchoring on reduced graphene oxide &amp; carbon (rGO&amp;C) nanosheets is synthesized through an in situ redox reaction.  The ethylenediamine and oxalic acid not only could induce the nucleation of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 along the surface of rGO, but also act as carbon sources of amorphous carbon, serving as binders to firmly and densely couple Na3V2(PO4)2F3 with the three-dimensional continuous conductive network constructed by rGO nanosheets.  The composite displays excellent rate capability and remarkable cycling stability (capacity retention of 81.9% for 1000 cycles at 30 C), due to the 2D rGO&amp;C nanosheets and anchored ultrafine Na3V2(PO4)2F3 nanoparticles shorten diffusion length of the ions and electrons, the firm connectivity between Na3V2(PO4)2F3 and rGO&amp;C nanosheets enables high structure stability to relieve the stress and strain generated during the cycling.  The strategy can be extended to prep. other NASICON vanadium phosphates cathodes materials for advanced batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.0c05490"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fiber-Shape Na3V2(PO4)2F3@N-Doped Carbon as a Cathode Material with Enhanced Cycling Stability for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunsha; Liang, Xinghui; Zhong, Guobin; Wang, Chao; Wu, Shijia; Xu, Kaiqi; Yang, Chenghao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

Herein, a comprehensive review of the recent research is presented to interpret the challenges and opportunities for the applications of HC anodes.  The ion storage mechanisms, materials design, and electrolyte optimizations for alkali metal-ion batteries are illustrated in-depth.  HC is particularly promising as an anode material for SIBs.  The solid-electrolyte interphase, initial Coulombic efficiency, safety concerns, and all-climate performances, which are vital for practical applications, are comprehensively discussed.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Constructing Heterostructured Bimetallic Selenides on an N-Doped Carbon Nanoframework as Anodes for Ultrastable Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Fei; Wang, Lei; Qin, Decai; Xu, Zhibin; Jin, Meiqi; Chen, Yu; Zeng, Xianxiang; Dai, Zhihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal selenides have been recognized as a class of promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) on account of their high capacity.  Nevertheless, the sluggish conversion kinetics and rapid capacity decay caused by insufficient cond. and vol. change restrain their applications.  Herein, hollow heterostructured bimetallic selenides embedded in an N-doped carbon nanoframework (H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC) were prepd. via a facile template-engaged method.  Benefiting from the rich defect at the phase boundary of the CoSe2/ZnSe heterostructure, pre-reserved cavity, and enhanced structure rigidity, the abovementioned issues are resolved at once, and the accelerated charge transportation kinetics traced by spectroscopy techniques and theor. calcns. certify the interface effect in the capacity release.  In addn., ex situ XPS, X-ray diffraction, and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy all confirm the high-reversible electrochem. conversion mechanism in H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC.  Together with a reasonable structural architecture and the highly reversible conversion reaction, H-CoSe2/ZnSe@NC displays a prominent rate capacity (244.8 mA h g-1 at 10 A g-1) as well as an ultralong lifespan (10,000 cycles at 10 A g-1), highlighting the significance of structure control in fabricating high-performance anodes for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c04647"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fluorine Dissolution-Induced Capacity Degradation for Fluorophosphate-Based Cathode Materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Long; Zhang, Na; Su, Yaqiong; Zhao, Jing; Song, Zhongxiao; Qian, Dan; Wu, Hu; Tahir, Muhammad; Saeed, Alam; Ding, Shujiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 has been considered as a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its high operating voltage and structural stability.  However, the issues about poor cycling performance and lack of understanding for the capacity degrdn. mechanism are the major hurdle for practical application.  Herein, we meticulously analyzed the evolution of the morphol., crystal structure, and bonding states of the cathode material during the cycling process.  We obsd. that capacity degrdn. is closely related to the shedding of the active material from the collector caused by HF corrosion.  Meanwhile, HF is produced through F anion dissoln. from Na3V2(PO4)2F3 induced by trace H2O during the cycling process.  The F- dissoln.-induced degrdn. mechanism based on fluorine-contg. cathode materials is proposed for the first time, providing a new insight for the understanding, modification, and performance improvement for fluorophosphate-based cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1149/2.0181805jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H. Interestingly, sodium ion distribution in augmented triangular prismatic sites of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is not unchanged, but shifts from the high energy Na(2)' site to the low energy Na(3)' site after a certain cycle, thus Na3V2(PO4)2F3 could obtain a higher energy d.  The full cell coupled with the composite cathode and Na metal anode constructed with Na-Sn alloy substrate exhibits excellent rate discharge capability and good cycling stability.  The nano-level carbon-PTHF double-coating developed in this work could provide a new way to improve Na+-storage and rate performance of Na-based materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2021.01.029"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y. In this work, we tried to clarify the misunderstandings about the NVPF compn. and structure with comprehensive investigation by sol-gel, solid-state and hydrothermal methods.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Optimizing high voltage Na3V2(PO4)2F3 cathode for achieving high rate sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Subramanian, Yuvaraj; Oh, Woong; Choi, Woosung; Lee, Hayeon; Jeong, Mihee; Thangavel, Ranjith; Yoon, Won-Sub</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have gained an intense attention as a promising alternate for Li-ion batteries due to their low cost, and abundant availability.  To meet high energy d. requirements, developing a high voltage cathode with ultra-long cycle life is of great importance.  Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) features a high working voltage, fast sodium-ion diffusion channels, and small vol. change during the cycling process.  However, the practical performance of NVPF cathode is currently hindered by poor Na+ ion diffusion at high voltage, low cycle life, and limited rate behavior.  Herein, we evaluate the effect of synthesis conditions in sol-gel technique, binders (PVDF, PAI and CMC), and electrolytes (ether, and ester based solvents) to overcome the diffusion limitation in high voltage NVPF cathode.  Benefiting from the synergistic effect of CMC binder, and DEGME electrolyte, and reduced graphene oxide composite, NVPF effectively overcome the potential barrier during Na+ ion insertion/extn. at high voltage.  NVPF with CMC binder and DEGDME electrolyte displayed a high Na+ ion diffusion kinetics, low cell resistance, and delivered an excellent electrochem. performance.  The current study provides new insights for overcoming the kinetic barrier during sodium ion storage in high voltage cathode that could direct the research development towards high energy sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c8ta00990b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C dispersed within carbon nanotube frameworks as a high tap density cathode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Chao; Long, Hai; Wang, Gencheng; Lu, Wei; Shao, Le; Xie, Keyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, the sodium-ion battery is one of the hottest topics in the field of battery research.  For practical application, however, high tap d., which is a key point of electrode materials, has always been ignored in previous studies.  Here, we present the fabrication of a NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C/CNT composite cathode with a high tap d. of 1.2 g cm-3 for high power and long lifespan sodium-ion batteries.  The spherical NVPF@C/CNTs synthesized through a spray drying method are composed of micron-sized primary particles dispersed within the intertwined carbon nanotube matrix.  The CNT framework not only provides an efficient elec. highway between primary particles, but also forms a stable mech. backbone for secondary particles.  The initial discharge capacity of NVPF@C/CNTs is about 113 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 1C, and the cell retains 98.2% after 300 cycles.  Besides, a high rate capacity of 85 mA h g-1 has been achieved at 30C.  We believe that our work presented here will be favorable for accelerating the commercialization of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.131780"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile strategy for developing uniform hierarchical sodium vanadium fluorophosphate@carbonized polyacrylonitrile multi-clustered hollow microspheres for high-energy-density sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Kang; Wang, Shijie; Zhao, Hongshun; Huang, Xiaobing; Ren, Yurong; He, Zhenjiang; Mao, Jing; Zheng, Junchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">428</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na superionic conductor structured Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) has received considerable attention as a cathode material for sodium-ion batteries because of its higher energy d. and three-dimensional open structure for Na+ diffusion channels.  However, its insulating structure [PO4] results in significantly inferior cond., which severely limits the electrochem. performance of NVPF.  In this study, uniform carbonized polyacrylonitrile-coated hierarchical Na3V2(PO4)2F3 multi-clustered hollow microspheres (NVPF-H@cPAN) were synthesized via a facile ethylene glycol-assisted hydrothermal approach, followed by a wet chem. method and heat treatment.  Further, the possible formation mechanism of hierarchical Na3V2(PO4)2F3 multi-clustered hollow microspheres was investigated.  The concn. of ethylene glycol and hydrothermal reaction time were found to play essential roles in the formation mechanism of the microspheres.  The as-prepd. NVPF-H@cPAN delivered a high discharge capacity of 116.2 mAh g-1 at 0.2C and impressive cycling stability of 85% at 5C after 2000 cycles.  When assembled as NVPF-H@cPAN||com. hard carbon (NVPF-H@cPAN||CHC) for sodium-ion full cells, which demonstrates a specific capacity of 107 mAh g-1 at 0.2C, thus achieving an energy d. of 376.4 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 141 W kg-1.  These results can be attributed to the structural regulation of multi-level clusters, which improved the Na+ diffusion rate and carbon coating strategy.  Such a combination of structural regulation and carbon-coating strategy can provide a strategy to synthesize materials with multi-level clusters of hollow microspheres to increase the electronic cond. and enhance the electrochem. performance of energy-storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1039/c7ra13441j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Assembly of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub>@C Nanoparticles in Reduced Graphene Oxide Enabling Superior Na<sup>+</sup> Storage for Symmetric Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2958</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2962</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Reduced graphene oxide (rGO) was used to encapsulate Na3V2(PO4)2F3@Carbon nanoparticles to overcome its inherent low electronic cond. and achieve superior sodium storage performance.  This as-prepd. cathode delivers a remarkable rate performance with a discharge capacity of ca. 64 mA h g-1 at 70C and an ultra-long-term cyclability over 4000 cycles with great capacity retention of 81% at 30C.  This excellent performance can be attributed to the favorable combination of fast ionic cond. of the NASICON structure and the interpenetrating conductive carbon framework; thus bringing a good pseudocapacitive quality to this material.  Furthermore, thanks to the good sodium storage properties at low potential, a sym. full cell can be assembled using Na3V2(PO4)2F3@C@rGO as both cathode and anode.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Templated Nanocrystal-Based Porous TiO2 Films for Next-Generation Electrochemical Capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Dunn, Bruce; Tolbert, Sarah H.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">131</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1802-1809</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages in using nanoscale materials for electrochem. energy storage are generally attributed to short diffusion path lengths for both electronic and lithium ion transport.  Here, another contribution, the charge storage from faradaic processes occurring at the surface, referred to as pseudocapacitive effect are considered.  This paper describes the synthesis and pseudocapacitive characteristics of block copolymer templated anatase TiO2 thin films synthesized using either sol-gel reagents or preformed nanocrystals as building blocks.  Both materials are highly cryst. and have large surface areas; however, the structure of the porosity is not identical.  The different titania systems were characterized by a combination of small- and wide-angle x-ray diffraction/scattering, combined with SEM imaging and physisorption measurements.  Following the authors' previously reported approach, the authors are able to use the voltammetric sweep rate dependence to det. quant. the capacitive contribution to the current response.  Considerable enhancement of the electrochem. properties results when the films are both made from nanocrystals and mesoporous.  Such materials show high levels of capacitive charge storage and high insertion capacities.  By contrast, when mesoscale porosity is created in a material with dense walls (rather than porous walls derived from the aggregation of nanocrystals), insertion capacities comparable to templated nanocrystal films can be achieved, but the capacitance is much lower.  The results presented here illustrate the importance of pseudocapacitive behavior that develops in high surface area mesoporous oxide films.  Such systems provide a new class of pseudocapacitive materials, which offer increased charge storage without compromising charge storage kinetics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1021/jp970490q"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lindström, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Södergren, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Solbrand, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rensmo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hjelm, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hagfeldt, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lindquist, S.-E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Li<sup>+</sup> Ion Insertion in TiO<sub>2</sub> (Anatase). 2.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The effect of carbon coating thickness on the capacity of LiFePO4/C composite cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cho, Yung-Da; Fey, George Ting-Kuo; Kao, Hsien-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">189</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two types of carbon source and precursor mixing pellets were employed simultaneously to prep. the LiFePO4/C composite materials: Type I using the LiFePO4 precursor with 20 wt.% polystyrene (PS) as a primary carbon source, and Type II using the LiFePO4 precursor with 50 wt.% malonic acid as a secondary carbon vapor source.  During final sintering, a Type I pellet was placed down-stream and Type II precursor pellet(s) was(were) placed upstream next to a Type I precursor pellet in a quartz-tube furnace.  The carbon-coated product of the sintered Type I precursor pellet was obtained by using both PS and malonic acid as carbon sources.  When two Type II pellets were used as a carbon vapor source (defined as Product-2), a more uniform film between 4 and 8 nm was formed, as shown in the TEM images.  In the absence of a secondary carbon source (defined as Product-0), the discharge capacity of Product-0 was 137 mAh g-1 with 100 cycles at a 0.2C-rate, but Product-2 demonstrated a high capacity of 151 mAh g-1 with 400 cycles.  Our results indicate that electrochem. properties of LiFePO4 are correlated to the amt. of carbon and its coating thickness and uniformity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-019-08359-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mariyappan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rousse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jacquet, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deschamps, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mirvaux, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Freeland, J. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tarascon, J.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Higher Energy and Safer Sodium Ion Batteries via an Electrochemically made Disordered Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Material</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">585</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41467-019-08359-y</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D585%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DG.%2BYan%26author%3DS.%2BMariyappan%26author%3DG.%2BRousse%26author%3DQ.%2BJacquet%26author%3DM.%2BDeschamps%26author%3DR.%2BDavid%26author%3DB.%2BMirvaux%26author%3DJ.%2BW.%2BFreeland%26author%3DJ.-M.%2BTarascon%26title%3DHigher%2BEnergy%2Band%2BSafer%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Bvia%2Ban%2BElectrochemically%2Bmade%2BDisordered%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BMaterial%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41467-019-08359-y&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c07897&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41467-019-08359-y&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Higher energy and safer sodium ion batteries via an electrochemically made disordered Na3V2(PO4)2F3 material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Guochun; Mariyappan, Sathiya; Rousse, Gwenaelle; Jacquet, Quentin; Deschamps, Michael; David, Renald; Mirvaux, Boris; Freeland, John William; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">585</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The growing need to store an increasing amt. of renewable energy in a sustainable way has rekindled interest for sodium-ion battery technol., owing to the natural abundance of sodium.  Presently, sodium-ion batteries based on Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C are the subject of intense research focused on improving the energy d. by harnessing the third sodium, which has so far been reported to be electrochem. inaccessible.  Here, we are able to trigger the activity of the third sodium electrochem. via the formation of a disordered NaxV2(PO4)2F3 phase of tetragonal symmetry (I4/mmm space group).  This phase can reversibly uptake 3 sodium ions per formula unit over the 1 to 4.8 V voltage range, with the last one being re-inserted at 1.6 V vs Na+/Na0.  We track the sodium-driven structural/charge compensation mechanism assocd. to the new phase and find that it remains disordered on cycling while its av. vanadium oxidn. state varies from 3 to 4.5.  Full sodium-ion cells based on this phase as pos. electrode and carbon as neg. electrode show a 10-20% increase in the overall energy d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1149/2.0181805jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon-Polytetrahydrofuran Double-Coated Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> Submicron-Composite as High-Energy/Power Cathode Material for Sodium Metal Battery</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>165</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">A746</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">A756</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/2.0181805jes</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D165%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3DA746-A756%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DH.%2BXiong%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BShao%26title%3DCarbon-Polytetrahydrofuran%2BDouble-Coated%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25292F3%2BSubmicron-Composite%2Bas%2BHigh-Energy%252FPower%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BMetal%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1149%252F2.0181805jes&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c07897&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F2.0181805jes&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Polytetrahydrofuran Double-Coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 Submicron-Composite as High-Energy/Power Cathode Material for Sodium Metal Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Hougao; Liu, Yutao; Yang, Yifu; Shao, Huixia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">165</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A746-A756</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A carbon-polytetrahydrofuran double-coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 composite has been prepd. by synthesis of carbon coated Na3V2(PO4)2F3 followed by in situ polymn. of THF on its surface.  Thermal gravimetry anal., Fourier transform IR spectrum and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy are used to confirm the encapsulation structure of the inner carbon layer and the outer polytetrahydrofuran layer on Na3V2(PO4)2F3.  Electrochem. tests show that electrochem. performance and electronic cond. of the composite are significantly improved due to the polytetrahydrofuran coating, and a reversible capacity of 123.6 mAh g-1 at a moderate 2 C rate is obtained with a high capacity retention of 98.5% after 250 cycles.  Even at an extremely high rate of 10 C the discharge capacity is still as high as 115.8 mAh g-1 with a capacity retention of 80% over 400 cycles.  Interestingly, sodium ion distribution in augmented triangular prismatic sites of Na3V2(PO4)2F3 is not unchanged, but shifts from the high energy Na(2)' site to the low energy Na(3)' site after a certain cycle, thus Na3V2(PO4)2F3 could obtain a higher energy d.  The full cell coupled with the composite cathode and Na metal anode constructed with Na-Sn alloy substrate exhibits excellent rate discharge capability and good cycling stability.  The nano-level carbon-PTHF double-coating developed in this work could provide a new way to improve Na+-storage and rate performance of Na-based materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref50" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/d0ta08634g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.                 10.1039/d0ta08634g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D24393-24400%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BH.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BK.%2BTang%26author%3DD.%2BZ.%2BJia%26author%3DY.%2BD.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BGuo%26author%3DZ.%2BZhou%26title%3DCarbon%2Bblock%2Banodes%2Bwith%2Bcolumnar%2Bnanopores%2Bconstructed%2Bfrom%2Bamine-functionalized%2Bcarbon%2Bnanosheets%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fd0ta08634g&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c07897&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fd0ta08634g&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon block anodes with columnar nanopores constructed from amine-functionalized carbon nanosheets for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yue; Zhang, Zihe; Tang, Yakun; Jia, Dianzeng; Huang, Yudai; Guo, Yong; Zhou, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24393-24400</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Earth-abundant sodium is a promising alternative to lithium in rechargeable batteries.  However, graphite, the com. anode material of lithium-ion batteries, cannot be used for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, carbon block anodes with columnar nanopores constructed from amine-functionalized carbon nanosheets were synthesized using modified polyacrylonitrile as the carbon source through a simple and economical low-temp. pyrolysis process, delivering high reversible capacity, superior rate capability and remarkable cyclic stability.  The surface-dominated redox reaction mechanism in Na storage is the origin of the fast kinetics, since the columnar nanopores which are considered as curled and sealed ultrathin nanosheets, like microjars, not only shorten the ion and electron diffusion length, but also expand the redox sites from the surface to the inner part.  This is similar to the storage mechanism in supercapacitors.  Moreover, d. functional theory computations reveal that the high-level amine groups play an important role in Na storage in the low potential region, endowing the block anode material with both high energy and power d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201701222"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.-E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.                 <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
